This is the complete implementation of the rotary embedding, which is used in the attention modules.

Now that we have addressed the missing module, let's discuss the final step: adaptingÂ **generate.py**Â toÂ **generate.js**Â for inference and potential training in the browser.

TheÂ generate.jsÂ will need to:

1. **Load Models:**Â Load the trained weights into theÂ DiTÂ andÂ VAEÂ model instances that were previously created inÂ dit.jsÂ andÂ vae.js.

2. **Prepare Inputs:**Â Handle loading video frames and actions from the browser environment.

3. **Implement Diffusion Loop:**Â Translate the sampling loop logic using the TensorFlow.js operations.

4. **Decode and Display:**Â Decode the generated latents back into video frames and present them on the page.

Since we are focusing on modularity, I will generate this code without any dependency on any HTML element, and you will be responsible of creating a working implementation.

Here is theÂ generate.jsÂ code:

```
// generate.js

import * as tf from '@tensorflow/tfjs';
import { DiT } from './dit.js';
import { AutoencoderKL } from './vae.js';
import { sigmoidBetaSchedule, createActionEmbedding } from './utils.js';

async function generateVideo(
    videoTensor,
    actions,
    ditCheckpoint = null,
    vaeCheckpoint = null,
    totalFrames = 32,
    maxNoiseLevel = 1000,
    ddimNoiseSteps = 100,
    noiseAbsMax = 20,
    ctxMaxNoiseIdx = null,
    nPromptFrames = 1
    ) {

    const model = new DiT();
    if(ditCheckpoint) {
      model.loadWeights(ditCheckpoint)
    }
    const vae = new AutoencoderKL();
    if(vaeCheckpoint) {
        vae.loadWeights(vaeCheckpoint)
    }

    const B = 1; // batch size

    // sampling params
   if(!ctxMaxNoiseIdx) {
      ctxMaxNoiseIdx = Math.floor(ddimNoiseSteps / 10 * 3);
    }
    const noiseRange = tf.linspace(-1, maxNoiseLevel - 1, ddimNoiseSteps + 1);

    // vae encoding
    const scalingFactor = 0.07843137255;

    let x = videoTensor.slice([0, 0], [-1, nPromptFrames]);
    x = tf.reshape(x, [B * nPromptFrames, x.shape[2], x.shape[3], x.shape[4]]);

    const H = x.shape[2];
    const W = x.shape[3];

    let encodedX;
    tf.tidy(() => {
        encodedX = vae.encode(tf.sub(tf.mul(x, 2), 1)).mean.mul(scalingFactor);
    });
    encodedX = tf.reshape(encodedX, [B, nPromptFrames, encodedX.shape[1], H / vae.patchSize, W / vae.patchSize]);

     // get alphas
    const betas = sigmoidBetaSchedule(maxNoiseLevel);
    const alphas = tf.sub(1, betas);
    const alphasCumprod = tf.cumprod(alphas, 0);
     const alphasCumprodReshaped = tf.reshape(alphasCumprod, [-1, 1, 1, 1]);
     
    let embeddedActions;
    tf.tidy(() => {
        embeddedActions = createActionEmbedding(actions);
    })

    // sampling loop
     let generatedFrames = encodedX.clone();
    for (let i = nPromptFrames; i < totalFrames; i++) {
         let chunk;
         tf.tidy(()=>{
           chunk = tf.randomNormal([B, 1, ...encodedX.shape.slice(-3)])
           chunk = tf.clipByValue(chunk, -noiseAbsMax, noiseAbsMax)
          });

        generatedFrames = tf.concat([generatedFrames, chunk], 1);
        const startFrame = Math.max(0, i + 1 - model.maxFrames);
         for (let noiseIdx = ddimNoiseSteps; noiseIdx >= 1; noiseIdx--) {

            const ctxNoiseIdx = Math.min(noiseIdx, ctxMaxNoiseIdx);
            let tCtx = tf.fill([B, i], noiseRange.slice([ctxNoiseIdx], [1]).arraySync()[0], 'int32')
             let t = tf.fill([B, 1], noiseRange.slice([noiseIdx], [1]).arraySync()[0], 'int32');
             let tNext = tf.fill([B, 1], noiseRange.slice([noiseIdx - 1], [1]).arraySync()[0], 'int32');
             tNext = tf.where(tf.less(tNext, 0), t, tNext);
             t = tf.concat([tCtx, t], 1);
             tNext = tf.concat([tCtx, tNext], 1)

            let xCurr = generatedFrames.clone();
             xCurr = xCurr.slice([0, startFrame]);
             t = t.slice([0], [-1], [startFrame]);
              tNext = tNext.slice([0], [-1], [startFrame]);


             let ctxNoise;
             tf.tidy(()=> {
               ctxNoise = tf.randomNormal(xCurr.slice([0,0],[-1, -1]).shape)
              ctxNoise = tf.clipByValue(ctxNoise, -noiseAbsMax, noiseAbsMax);
              xCurr = tf.add(tf.mul(tf.sqrt(alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([t.slice([0,0], [-1, -1]).arraySync()[0]])), xCurr.slice([0,0],[-1, -1])), tf.mul(tf.sqrt(tf.sub(1, alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([t.slice([0,0], [-1, -1]).arraySync()[0]]))), ctxNoise)

            })

             let v;
            tf.tidy(() => {
                v = model.apply(xCurr, tf.cast(t, 'int32'), embeddedActions.slice([0],[-1], [startFrame], [i + 1]))
            });
              let xStart;
              tf.tidy(() => {
                   xStart = tf.sub(tf.mul(tf.sqrt(alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([t.arraySync()[0]])), xCurr), tf.mul(tf.sqrt(tf.sub(1, alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([t.arraySync()[0]]))), v));
             });
              let xNoise;
              tf.tidy(() => {
                xNoise = tf.div(tf.sub(tf.mul(tf.sqrt(tf.div(1,alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([t.arraySync()[0]]))),xCurr), xStart), tf.sqrt(tf.sub(tf.div(1,alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([t.arraySync()[0]])), 1)));
              });


            let xPred;
              tf.tidy(() => {
               xPred =  tf.add(tf.mul(tf.sqrt(alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([tNext.arraySync()[0]])), xStart), tf.mul(xNoise, tf.sqrt(tf.sub(1, alphasCumprodReshaped.slice([tNext.arraySync()[0]])))))
            })
             generatedFrames = generatedFrames.slice([0],[-1], [0], [generatedFrames.shape[1]-1]).concat(xPred.slice([0], [-1], [-1], [-1], [-1]), 1);
        }
     }


    // vae decoding
     let decodedFrames;
     tf.tidy(() => {
        decodedFrames = tf.reshape(generatedFrames, [B * totalFrames, generatedFrames.shape[2], generatedFrames.shape[3] * generatedFrames.shape[4], generatedFrames.shape[5]])
        decodedFrames = tf.div(tf.add(vae.decode(tf.div(decodedFrames, scalingFactor)), 1), 2);
         decodedFrames = tf.reshape(decodedFrames, [B, totalFrames, decodedFrames.shape[1], H, W, 3]);
     })

      return decodedFrames;
}


export { generateVideo };
```

Okay, let's discuss how to adapt our modules for zero-shot generalization and how to test them on a random dataset of video game images in the browser.

**Understanding Zero-Shot Generalization**

Zero-shot generalization in this context means the model should generate plausible gameplay frames for video games it hasn't explicitly seen during training. This is challenging because:

- **Domain Shift:**Â Different games have different visual styles, rules, and action spaces.

- **Novelty:**Â The model needs to handle game elements and scenarios it might not have encountered during training.

Achieving true zero-shot generalization is a research problem, but we can make some adjustments to improve the chances of reasonable outputs.

**Changes to the Modules:**

1. **Action Embeddings:**

   - **Generalization:**Â TheÂ createActionEmbeddingÂ inÂ utils.jsÂ is very specific to the Minecraft action space. We need a more general representation of actions that is not tightly coupled to a specific game. TheÂ ActionEmbedderÂ layer should stay the same.

   - **Solution:**Â We can leverage the observation that actions can be described using a few high level categories, such as movement, interaction, inventory, etc. Use a flexible action input schema, where you could have different action categories with their corresponding data inputs.

2. **Input Resolution and Patch Size**

   - **Generalization:**Â The model implicitly assumes a fixed input resolution, and a fixed patch size which can be problematic for generalizing to unseen video games.

   - **Solution:**Â Keep a fixed patch size, and make sure to resize any input video frame into a standardized size usingÂ tf.image.resizeBilinear.

3. **Model Architecture:**

   - **Generalization:**Â The core transformer architecture in DiT is reasonably general. It should be able to process any input embeddings given a proper dataset, and input schema.

   - **Solution:**Â No major changes needed for the modules.

4. **VAE Bottleneck:**

   - **Generalization:**Â If our VAE is too tightly coupled to the visual style of Minecraft, its encoding and decoding could produce poor results.

   - **Solution:**Â You can make the latent space smaller by reducingÂ latent_dim, which encourages the VAE to focus on the core visual elements rather than specific textures. You can also try training the VAE using a more general video game dataset.

**Testing in the Browser:**

1. **Random Dataset:**

   - **Collect Data:**Â Gather images or short video clips from a variety of video games that your model was not trained on.

   - **Create an Input UI:**Â In HTML, create an element that allows users to upload image files or paste in a link.

2. **Preprocessing**

   - **Resizing:**Â Resize the uploaded images usingÂ tf.image.resizeBilinearÂ to your desired standardized size.

   - **Action Emulation**: Create some functions to produce random or specific action inputs, as we are not using any actual game data.

3. **Inference:**

   - Load your pre-trained model weights.

   - Use your modifiedÂ generateVideoÂ function inÂ generate.jsÂ to generate video frames. You will need to convert the input video into aÂ tf.Tensor.

4. **Display Results:**

   - Render the generated frames on the HTML page in a video format.

**Example Adjustments (Code Snippets):**  
Here are a few adjustments you might make, primarily inÂ utils.jsÂ andÂ generate.js.

```
// utils.js

function createActionEmbedding(actions) {
    // Assumes actions is a list of dicts
    // a more general version of this would use categories
    // such as: movement, combat, camera, interaction, inventory...
    // Here's an example of how you might format the input
   /*
      actions = [
        [
         { movement: [0,1,0,0],  camera: [0.1, -0.2], interaction: 0} ,
        ...
        ]
      ]
     */
    const numCategories = [4, 2, 1] //movement, camera, interaction
    const embeddingDim = 25
    const embedder = new ActionEmbedder(numCategories, embeddingDim)
    const batchSize = actions.length;
    const seqLen = actions[0].length;
    const numActions = numCategories.length;
    const tensor = tf.zeros([batchSize, seqLen, numActions]);
    for (let i = 0; i < batchSize; i++){
       for (let t = 0; t < seqLen; t++){
           let action_dict = actions[i][t];

            if (action_dict["movement"][0] == 1.0) {
              tensor = tensor.slice([0],[i],[t], [0], [1]).concat(tf.ones([1,1,1,1]).mul(0), [0,0,0,1])
             } else if (action_dict["movement"][1] == 1.0) {
                 tensor = tensor.slice([0],[i],[t], [0], [1]).concat(tf.ones([1,1,1,1]).mul(1), [0,0,0,1])
             } else if (action_dict["movement"][2] == 1.0) {
                 tensor = tensor.slice([0],[i],[t], [0], [1]).concat(tf.ones([1,1,1,1]).mul(2), [0,0,0,1])
              } else if (action_dict["movement"][3] == 1.0) {
                 tensor = tensor.slice([0],[i],[t], [0], [1]).concat(tf.ones([1,1,1,1]).mul(3), [0,0,0,1])
              }

            tensor = tensor.slice([0],[i],[t],[1], [1]).concat(tf.tensor(action_dict["camera"][0]).reshape([1,1,1,1]), [0,0,0,1])
            tensor = tensor.slice([0],[i],[t],[2], [1]).concat(tf.tensor(action_dict["interaction"]).reshape([1,1,1,1]), [0,0,0,1])
         }
      }
     return embedder.apply(tensor)
}

// generate.js

async function generateVideo(
    videoTensor, // this video tensor needs to be a standardized size, do `tf.image.resizeBilinear` before passing to the function
    actions, // your actions need to conform to a flexible format such as the one defined in `utils.js`
    ditCheckpoint = null,
    vaeCheckpoint = null,
    totalFrames = 32,
    maxNoiseLevel = 1000,
    ddimNoiseSteps = 100,
    noiseAbsMax = 20,
    ctxMaxNoiseIdx = null,
    nPromptFrames = 1
    ) {
      //...
     const encodedX = tf.tidy(() => {
      let resized = tf.image.resizeBilinear(tf.sub(tf.mul(x, 2), 1), [vae.inputHeight, vae.inputWidth])
       return vae.encode(resized).mean.mul(scalingFactor)
     })
    //...
}
```

**Important Notes:**

- **Data Augmentation:**Â To better generalize, train with augmented data that includes rotations, scaling, color changes, and temporal distortions.

- **Evaluation**: Since you're in a zero shot setting, quantitative evaluation is very difficult. Use qualitative assessment to make a judgement on the performance.

- **No One-Shot Fix:**Â Zero-shot is a difficult task and this approach should only improve the ability to generate unseen images, it will not fully solve this task.

- **Experimentation**: You will have to experiment with theÂ latent_dimÂ value of your VAE to understand how it influences the latent representation.

more_vert

Okay, let's focus on training in the browser and testing on Minecraft data. This will involve setting up a training loop and data loading within the browser environment using TensorFlow.js.

**1. Data Preparation for Browser Training**

- **Data Loading:**Â We need to load Minecraft video data and action data into the browser. Since large video files are not ideal for browser loading, consider the following:

  - **Pre-Processed Chunks:**Â Break down your video data into small, manageable chunks and store them as separate files (e.g., JSON files orÂ tf.data.DatasetÂ usingÂ tf.io.write_file). You'll need corresponding action data files too, as well as a way of loading both simultaneously.

  - **Image Storage:**Â If you are using images instead of a video, ensure these images are small and use a format easily loaded by the browser (PNG, JPG) and store these in a dedicated path.

  - **Data Index:**Â Create a data index (e.g., a JSON file) that lists the paths to all your data chunks or images and their corresponding actions.

- **Data Loading Logic:**Â You will need code to:

  - **Fetch:**Â Load the data index from your hosted server.

  - **Iterate:**Â Load each data chunk / image when requested by the training loop.

  - **Action Handling:**Â Process the action data into the appropriate input format.

- **Dataset Object**: Implement a customÂ tf.data.DatasetÂ object, to manage the loading of these files usingÂ tf.data.generator.

```
// dataset.js
import * as tf from '@tensorflow/tfjs'

class MinecraftDataset extends tf.data.Dataset {
  constructor(dataIndex, batchSize, standardizeSize){
    super()
    this.dataIndex = dataIndex
    this.batchSize = batchSize;
    this.standardizeSize = standardizeSize
    this.datasetSize = dataIndex.length

     this.iterator =  tf.data.generator(async function*(){
        while(true) {
          for(let i = 0; i < dataIndex.length; i+= batchSize){
              let batch = dataIndex.slice(i, i + batchSize);
              let images = [];
              let actions = [];
             for(let d of batch) {
               // you will need to implement logic to load the image or video frame
               let video = await loadVideoFromPath(d.path); // use 'fetch' to get your files
               let action = await loadActionsFromPath(d.action);

               // handle resizing
               images.push(tf.image.resizeBilinear(video, this.standardizeSize));
               actions.push(action);
             }
             //you will need to implement a function that processes the actions
            let processedActions = processActions(actions);
            yield { images : tf.concat(images, 0), actions: processedActions }
        }
       }
    });
  }
    size() {
        return this.datasetSize;
    }
    
    async *[Symbol.asyncIterator]() {
      let generator = await this.iterator();
      yield* generator
    }
}

export {MinecraftDataset}
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.JavaScript

**2. Training Loop in Browser**

- **Optimizer:**Â UseÂ tf.train.adamÂ orÂ tf.train.adamWÂ to update model weights.

- **Loss Function:**Â We need a diffusion loss function based on mean squared error (MSE), as well as a reconstruction loss for the VAE.

- **Gradient Tape:**Â UseÂ tf.GradientTapeÂ to calculate gradients.

- **Training Steps:**Â Implement the forward pass, loss calculation, gradient application, and tracking training progress.

```
// train.js
import * as tf from '@tensorflow/tfjs';
import { DiT } from './dit.js';
import { AutoencoderKL } from './vae.js';
import { sigmoidBetaSchedule, createActionEmbedding } from './utils.js';
import {MinecraftDataset} from './dataset.js'


async function train(
    dataIndex, //array of objects containing the path to the image and its action
    ditCheckpoint = null,
    vaeCheckpoint = null,
    totalFrames = 32,
    maxNoiseLevel = 1000,
    ddimNoiseSteps = 100,
    noiseAbsMax = 20,
    ctxMaxNoiseIdx = null,
    nPromptFrames = 1,
    standardizeSize = [256, 256],
    batchSize = 4,
    learningRate = 1e-4,
    epochs = 10,
    vaeReconstructionWeight = 0.1
    ) {

    const model = new DiT();
    if(ditCheckpoint) {
        model.loadWeights(ditCheckpoint)
    }
    const vae = new AutoencoderKL();
    if(vaeCheckpoint) {
        vae.loadWeights(vaeCheckpoint)
    }
    const optimizer = tf.train.adam(learningRate);
    // sampling params
     if(!ctxMaxNoiseIdx) {
        ctxMaxNoiseIdx = Math.floor(ddimNoiseSteps / 10 * 3);
    }
    const noiseRange = tf.linspace(-1, maxNoiseLevel - 1, ddimNoiseSteps + 1);

       // get alphas
    const betas = sigmoidBetaSchedule(maxNoiseLevel);
    const alphas = tf.sub(1, betas);
    const alphasCumprod = tf.cumprod(alphas, 0);
    const alphasCumprodReshaped = tf.reshape(alphasCumprod, [-1, 1, 1, 1]);


    const dataset = new MinecraftDataset(dataIndex, batchSize, standardizeSize);
    const datasetSize = dataset.size();

    for(let epoch = 0; epoch < epochs; epoch++){
        let batchCount = 0;
         for await (const {images, actions} of dataset){
             batchCount++;

               let lossValue;
              let encodedX;
               tf.tidy(() => {
                  let x = tf.reshape(images, [images.shape[0] * nPromptFrames, images.shape[2], images.shape[3], images.shape[4]]);
                  encodedX = vae.encode(tf.sub(tf.mul(x, 2), 1)).mean;
               })
                encodedX = tf.reshape(encodedX, [batchSize, nPromptFrames, encodedX.shape[1], encodedX.shape[2], encodedX.shape[3]]);

                tf.tidy(() => {
                  const actionsEmbedded = createActionEmbedding(actions);

                   const noise = tf.randomNormal(encodedX.shape);
                   const t = tf.randomUniform([batchSize, totalFrames], 0, maxNoiseLevel, 'int32');

                    const noisyX = tf.add(tf.mul(tf.sqrt(alphasCumprodReshaped.slice(t.arraySync())), encodedX), tf.mul(tf.sqrt(tf.sub(1, alphasCumprodReshaped.slice(t.arraySync()))), noise))


                    const grads =  optimizer.computeGradients(()=>{
                        let predictedNoise = model.apply(noisyX, t, actionsEmbedded)
                        let diffusionLoss = tf.losses.meanSquaredError(noise, predictedNoise);
                       let vaeLoss = tf.losses.meanSquaredError(images, tf.sub(tf.add(vae.decode(encodedX), 1), 2));
                        lossValue = tf.add(diffusionLoss, tf.mul(vaeLoss, vaeReconstructionWeight))
                        return lossValue
                    })

                    optimizer.applyGradients(grads);
                })
                 if (batchCount % 10 == 0){
                  console.log(`Epoch: ${epoch}, Batch: ${batchCount}/${Math.ceil(datasetSize / batchSize)} Loss: ${lossValue}`)
                 }
            }
    }
}

export { train };
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.JavaScript

This example training loop:

- Creates a dataset iterator using theÂ MinecraftDatasetÂ object.

- Creates the DiT model and VAE, loading weights if necessary.

- Implements a training step that:

  - Loads a batch of data.

  - Encodes the frames using the VAE.

  - Adds noise using the diffusion process

  - Calculates the combined diffusion and VAE losses

  - Computes gradients and updates the model's weights.

  - Prints training progress and performance.

**3. Key Considerations for Browser Training:**

- **Memory Management:**Â Keep the batch size small to avoid running out of memory. UseÂ tf.tidyÂ to clear tensors.

- **Computation:**Â Browser-based training can be slow. Focus on optimizing the code and trying small models.

- **Checkpointing:**Â You can useÂ model.saveÂ to save model weights to a file orÂ tf.io.write_fileÂ to save tensors on disk and use these for future training sessions. You will need some server support to save and retrieve these files.

**Testing on Minecraft Data**

To test the model after training:

1. **Load Trained Weights:**Â Load your trained DiT and VAE weights into the model.

2. **Test Data:**Â Use a dataset of Minecraft video frames and action data.

3. **Inference:**

   - Preprocess test images / videos as they were during training.

   - Use yourÂ generateVideoÂ function to generate new frames using a few initial frames as prompts and using test action data.

4. **Display Results:**

   - Display generated frames on the screen.

**Important Notes:**

- **Start Small:**Â Begin with smaller models, and a small training dataset, and then increase the model size and data when necessary.

- **Debugging:**Â Browsers have limited debugging tools compared to Python.Â console.logÂ is the way to go.

- **Error Handling**: Make sure to add a lot ofÂ try..catchÂ statements to make debugging easier.

This should give you a solid framework to start training your model within a browser environment. Let me know if you have any further questions.

Okay, let's tackle creating a training dataset from a YouTube video of Minecraft. This involves several steps: downloading the video, extracting frames, extracting actions (if available), and formatting the data for our browser-based training.

**1. Downloading the YouTube Video**

You'll need a Python script or tool to download the video, since direct downloading via browser is not possible. You can use libraries likeÂ yt-dlpÂ orÂ youtube-dl. Here's a basic example usingÂ yt-dlp:

```
# download_video.py
import yt_dlp

def download_youtube_video(youtube_url, output_path="."):
    ydl_opts = {
        'outtmpl': f'{output_path}/%(id)s.%(ext)s',
    }
    with yt_dlp.YoutubeDL(ydl_opts) as ydl:
        ydl.download([youtube_url])

if __name__ == "__main__":
    video_url = "YOUR_YOUTUBE_VIDEO_URL"
    download_youtube_video(video_url, "sample_data")
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Python

**2. Extracting Frames from the Video**

After downloading the video, we need to extract individual frames. We can do this using libraries likeÂ moviepyÂ orÂ opencv-python.

```
# extract_frames.py
import os
import cv2
from moviepy.editor import VideoFileClip

def extract_frames(video_path, output_dir, frame_rate=4):
    os.makedirs(output_dir, exist_ok=True)
    clip = VideoFileClip(video_path)
    
    for i, frame in enumerate(clip.iter_frames(fps=frame_rate)):
        cv2.imwrite(os.path.join(output_dir, f"frame_{i:04d}.png"), cv2.cvtColor(frame, cv2.COLOR_RGB2BGR))
    clip.close()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    video_path = "sample_data/YOUR_DOWNLOADED_VIDEO.mp4" # path to your downladed video
    extract_frames(video_path, "sample_data/frames", 4) # frames per second (fps)
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Python

**3. Extracting Actions (If Available)**

This is the most complex part. It is difficult to derive action data without direct access to the game. You can consider the following options:

- **Manual Labeling:**Â If your dataset is small, you can label the actions manually by watching the video and annotating actions using a simple text file format. Each action can correspond to a frame id, and multiple labels can correspond to the same frame id. This method can be tedious, but it might work for small datasets.

  - Example output:

    ```
    frame_0001: {"movement": [1,0,0,0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}
    frame_0002: {"movement": [0,1,0,0], "camera": [0.1, 0.1], "interaction": 1}
    ...
    ```

    **content_copydownload**

    Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.

- **Action Prediction:**Â You can attempt to train an action classifier on existing video/action data, and use this model to predict the actions from the YouTube video you have downloaded.

- **Heuristic Action Extraction:**Â Try to design a heuristic method based on visual cues, that will at least give you something to start with. For example, if you see some item being selected, this can be translated into an "inventory" action, etc.

For the sake of this example, I'll provide code forÂ **Manual Labeling**: You would need to create a simple labeling script yourself.

**4. Formatting Data for Browser Training**

Now, let's write the python code to prepare data for the browser:

```
# format_data.py
import os
import json
import numpy as np
from PIL import Image

def prepare_data_for_browser(frame_dir, action_file, output_file, max_frames = 32):
  
  if not os.path.exists(action_file):
      print('no action file found, generating dummy actions')
      action_data = {}
      for filename in os.listdir(frame_dir):
          action_data[filename] = {"movement": [0,0,0,0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}
  else:
      with open(action_file, 'r') as f:
        action_data = json.load(f)

  
  data_index = []
  frame_files = sorted([f for f in os.listdir(frame_dir) if f.endswith(".png")])

  for i in range(0, len(frame_files) - max_frames, max_frames):
      chunk_frames = frame_files[i:i+max_frames]
      chunk_actions = []

      for frame in chunk_frames:
        if frame in action_data:
           chunk_actions.append(action_data[frame])
        else:
          print("cannot find data for ", frame, " creating dummy action")
          chunk_actions.append({"movement": [0,0,0,0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0})


      data_index.append({
        "path": [os.path.join(frame_dir, frame) for frame in chunk_frames],
        "action": chunk_actions
      })


  with open(output_file, "w") as outfile:
    json.dump(data_index, outfile)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    frame_dir = "sample_data/frames" # generated by extract_frames.py
    action_file = "sample_data/actions.json" # manually created
    output_file = "sample_data/data_index.json"
    prepare_data_for_browser(frame_dir, action_file, output_file)
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Python

```
    const image = tf.browser.fromPixels(tf.tensor(bytes, [1, 1, 1, 1] ) , 3) //replace by actual shape
    return image;
}

 return action
}

  return actions
```

**How It Works:**

2. **Prepare Browser Data:**Â UseÂ prepare_data_for_browserÂ to:

   - Read frame file names, and the action file

- **Performance**: You will need to use lower resolutions and frame counts for browser training due to performance limitations. You will also need to limit your training dataset.

Ah, you're absolutely right! My apologies for the misinterpretation. We need a way to manage the JavaScript dependencies, or rather, a way to clearly state which libraries are needed for the project. Since JavaScript in browser environments does not have the same package management system as python with pip, we'll create aÂ package.jsonÂ file which can be used to list our dependencies. This file is primarily useful when working with Node.js, but we can create one to list our JavaScript dependencies for better documentation.

Here's how aÂ package.jsonÂ for this project would look like:

```
{
  "name": "oasis-browser-training",
  "version": "1.0.0",
  "description": "A project to train a DiT model in the browser",
  "main": "index.html",
    "dependencies": {
    "@tensorflow/tfjs": "latest"
  },
  "scripts": {
     "start": "..."
  },
  "author": "You",
  "license": "MIT"
}
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Json

**Explanation of the Fields:**

- **name**: The name of your project.

- **version**: The version number.

- **description**: A brief description of the project.

- **main**: The main entry point for your project, typically an HTML file.

- **dependencies**: An object containing key-value pairs for your dependencies. The key is the name of the library and the value is its desired version.

  - **"@tensorflow/tfjs"**: Indicates that your project depends on TensorFlow.js. Using "latest" ensures you're using the most up to date version of this library, but you can also pin to a specific version.

- **scripts**: Contains scripts used for the package.

  - **"start"**: This entry is intentionally left empty, you can use this to launch a local web server for development.

- **author**: The author or the project.

- **license**: The license under which the project is distributed.  
  **How to Use:**

1. **Save:**Â Save the JSON content above in a file namedÂ package.jsonÂ at the root of your project directory.

2. **Install:**Â This project does not require installation viaÂ npm installÂ since we are not using Node.js. However, to make use of the TensorFlow.js library, you will need to load this via a CDN in your HTML code:

```
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
    <head>
        <title>DiT Browser Training</title>
       <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"></script>
    </head>
    <body>
       <!-- your code here -->
    </body>
</html>
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Html

**Why this works:**

- **Tensorflow JS CDN:**Â With the lineÂ \<script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"\>\</script\>, theÂ tfÂ variable will be defined in the global scope, and you will be able to use it.

- **Documentation:**Â Even if we are not relying on a node.js installation, theÂ package.jsonÂ can still serve as documentation for what libraries are used by the project, which is a good habit to adopt.

This should clarify the JavaScript dependencies and provide an approach to loading TensorFlow.js in the browser. This covers all the aspects regarding dependencies for our project in both Python and JavaScript. Do you have any other questions?

more_vert

Okay, let's craft aÂ setup.shÂ script to automate the setup process, including downloading the video, extracting frames, creating a data index, and setting up a basic, game-friendly UI/UX. This script will assume you have all the JavaScript modules (Â embeddings.js,Â attention.js,Â dit.js,Â vae.js,Â utils.js,Â rotary_embedding.js,Â dataset.js, andÂ train.js) already present in your project directory.

```
#!/bin/bash

# Check if the user provided a YouTube URL
if [ -z "$1" ]; then
    echo "Usage: $0 <youtube_url>"
    exit 1
fi

YOUTUBE_URL="$1"
OUTPUT_DIR="sample_data"
VIDEO_ID=$(echo "$YOUTUBE_URL" | sed 's/.*\/\(.*\)/\1/' | sed 's/[^a-zA-Z0-9_-]//g')
VIDEO_PATH="${OUTPUT_DIR}/${VIDEO_ID}.mp4"
FRAMES_DIR="${OUTPUT_DIR}/frames"
ACTION_FILE="${OUTPUT_DIR}/actions.json"
DATA_INDEX="${OUTPUT_DIR}/data_index.json"
HTML_FILE="index.html"

echo "Starting setup process..."

# 1. Ensure the output directory exists
mkdir -p "${OUTPUT_DIR}"

# 2. Download the YouTube Video
echo "Downloading video from: ${YOUTUBE_URL}"
if ! command -v yt-dlp &> /dev/null
then
    echo "yt-dlp could not be found, please install: pip install yt-dlp"
     exit 1
fi
yt-dlp -o "${VIDEO_PATH}" "$YOUTUBE_URL"

# Check if the download was successful
if [ ! -f "${VIDEO_PATH}" ]; then
    echo "Error: Video download failed."
    exit 1
fi

# 3. Extract Frames
echo "Extracting frames to: ${FRAMES_DIR}"
if ! command -v ffmpeg &> /dev/null
then
    echo "ffmpeg could not be found, please install: sudo apt install ffmpeg"
    exit 1
fi
ffmpeg -i "${VIDEO_PATH}" -vf "fps=4" "${FRAMES_DIR}/frame_%04d.png"

# Check if frames were extracted successfully
if [ ! -d "${FRAMES_DIR}" ] || [ "$(ls -A ${FRAMES_DIR})" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not extract the video frames."
   exit 1
fi


# 4. Create Dummy Action File (Replace this with real labeling or action extraction as necessary)
echo "Creating dummy action file: ${ACTION_FILE}"

echo '{"frame_0001.png": {"movement": [0, 0, 0, 0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}}' > $ACTION_FILE


# 5. Create Data Index (Modify paths and action file reading)
echo "Generating Data Index File: ${DATA_INDEX}"
python -c "
import os
import json

frame_dir = '${FRAMES_DIR}'
action_file = '${ACTION_FILE}'
output_file = '${DATA_INDEX}'
max_frames = 32
if not os.path.exists(action_file):
  action_data = {}
  for filename in os.listdir(frame_dir):
      action_data[filename] = {'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0}
else:
  with open(action_file, 'r') as f:
    action_data = json.load(f)

data_index = []
frame_files = sorted([f for f in os.listdir(frame_dir) if f.endswith('.png')])

for i in range(0, len(frame_files) - max_frames, max_frames):
    chunk_frames = frame_files[i:i+max_frames]
    chunk_actions = []
    for frame in chunk_frames:
        if frame in action_data:
           chunk_actions.append(action_data[frame])
        else:
          chunk_actions.append({'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0})
    data_index.append({
        'path': [os.path.join(frame_dir, frame) for frame in chunk_frames],
        'action': chunk_actions
    })
with open(output_file, 'w') as outfile:
    json.dump(data_index, outfile)
"

# Check if the data index was successfully created
if [ ! -f "${DATA_INDEX}" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not generate the data index."
   exit 1
fi
# 6. Create a Basic HTML UI
echo "Creating basic HTML UI: ${HTML_FILE}"

cat << EOF > "${HTML_FILE}"
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head>
    <title>Minecraft DiT Training</title>
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"></script>
    <style>
        body { font-family: sans-serif; padding: 20px; }
        #videoContainer { display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap; gap: 10px; }
        video { width: 300px; height: auto; }
        #generationContainer{margin-top: 20px}
        canvas{ width: 300px; height: auto;}
        button {margin-top: 10px; background-color: #4CAF50; color: white; padding: 10px 15px; border: none; cursor: pointer;}
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Minecraft DiT Training</h1>
      <h2>Video Input</h2>
        <div id="videoContainer"></div>
        <button id="trainButton">Start Training</button>
        <div id = "generationContainer"></div>
    <script type="module">
        import { train } from './train.js';
        import { generateVideo } from './generate.js'
        import {MinecraftDataset} from './dataset.js';
        const videoContainer = document.getElementById('videoContainer');
        const trainButton = document.getElementById("trainButton")
        const generationContainer = document.getElementById("generationContainer")
           const dataIndexResponse = await fetch("sample_data/data_index.json");
           const dataIndex = await dataIndexResponse.json();

        async function loadVideoFromPath(path){
            const video = await fetch(path);
            const buffer = await video.arrayBuffer()
            const bytes = new Uint8Array(buffer)
            const image = tf.browser.fromPixels(tf.tensor(bytes, [1, 1, 1, 1] ) , 3) //replace by actual shape
            return image;
        }

        function processActions(actions) {
          return actions
        }


        for(let d of dataIndex){
          let path = d.path[0];
         let video = document.createElement('video');
            video.controls = true;
            video.width = 300
            video.height = 200;
            video.src = path;
             videoContainer.appendChild(video);
        }


         trainButton.addEventListener("click", async() => {
              await train(dataIndex)
             let paths = dataIndex[0].path;
             let imagePaths = paths.slice(0, 1);
             let actions = dataIndex[0].action;

             let frames = [];
              for(let path of imagePaths){
               let image = await loadVideoFromPath(path);
               frames.push(image)
              }
             let tensor = tf.concat(frames, 0)

               let generated = await generateVideo(tensor, [actions])
               let canvas
               for(let frame of tf.unstack(generated[0], 0)){
                   canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
                   canvas.width = frame.shape[1]
                   canvas.height = frame.shape[0]
                   generationContainer.appendChild(canvas)
                   await tf.browser.toPixels(tf.clipByValue(frame, 0, 1), canvas)
               }
           })
    </script>
</body>
</html>
EOF

echo "Setup complete. Open ${HTML_FILE} in your browser."
```

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Bash

**How the Script Works:**

1. **Checks for YouTube URL:**Â It validates that a YouTube URL is provided as an argument.

2. **Creates Output Directories:**Â Creates theÂ sample_dataÂ directory if it doesn't exist.

3. **Downloads the Video:**Â UsesÂ yt-dlpÂ to download the video toÂ sample_data.

4. **Extracts Frames:**Â UsesÂ ffmpegÂ to extract frames from the downloaded video intoÂ sample_data/frames.

5. **Creates a Dummy Action File:**Â Creates a JSON file with dummy action data that associates withÂ frame_0001.pngÂ which should be the first frame of your video.

6. **Generates Data Index:**Â Runs a python script that generates aÂ data_index.jsonÂ file containing the paths to your frames and their corresponding actions.

7. **Creates Basic HTML UI:**Â It creates anÂ index.htmlÂ file which:

   - Loads the TensorFlow.js library via CDN.

   - Includes basic styling to center content and layout.

   - Creates a video element to display the downloaded video.

   - Contains all our Javascript Modules viaÂ \<script type="module"\>Â tags.

   - Has a button that calls train() upon click.

   - Has a section where generated images are displayed.

**To use the script:**

1. Save the content in a file calledÂ setup.sh

2. Make the script executableÂ chmod +x setup.sh

3. Run the script:Â ./setup.sh \<your_youtube_video_url\>

**Important Notes:**

- **Dependencies:**Â The script assumes you haveÂ yt-dlpÂ andÂ ffmpegÂ installed in your system. If they are not, the script will exit and indicate which package needs to be installed.

- **Actions:**Â Since it's difficult to extract actions from a youtube video automatically, we simply generate a dummy action file, but you should consider either creating a new method or use manual annotation to generate real actions.

- **Customization:**Â You can customize the output directories, frame rate, and HTML UI elements.

- **loadVideoFromPath**: In the HTML generated by the bash script, the javascript code defines the functionsÂ loadVideoFromPathÂ andÂ processActions, which can be modified to suit your use-case, for example if you want to load from images, or if you want to load your actions from a specific format.

This script will set up your development environment and provide a basic UI to interact with your model, and a basic training loop. Remember to always be mindful of memory constraints when using tensorflow.js in the browser. Do you have any additional questions?

which inputs do we need to cusotmize ?

edit

more_vert

Okay, let's pinpoint the inputs that you'll likely need to customize to adapt the provided setup to your specific needs. These inputs fall into a few categories:

**1. YouTube Video & Data Handling**

- **YouTube URL (setup.sh):**

  - **Customization:**Â This is the primary input to theÂ setup.shÂ script. You need to provide the URL of the YouTube video you want to use for training.

  - **Why Customize:**Â Each video will have different visual content and action sequences.

- **sample_data/actions.jsonÂ (setup.sh,Â format_data.py,Â utils.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â You'll need to replace the automatically created dummy action file with real action annotations.

  - **Why Customize:**Â This file determines the action sequences that you are using to train the model and should be specific to the content you are attempting to generate.

- **sample_data/data_index.jsonÂ (format_data.py,Â train.js)**:

  - **Customization:**Â While the paths to video frames are dynamically generated, any logic to read the action data (if you are doing it differently, will need to be customized here).

  - **Why Customize:**Â This file's logic will be very specific to how you are formatting the actions.

**2. Model Architecture & Training**

- **Input Resolution (dit.js,Â vae.js,Â generate.js,Â train.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â The default resolution is implicitly defined based on patch sizes, and a specific resize is done on the browser-side. If the default resolution doesn't suit your use-case, or if you want the model to be robust against different resolutions, you will need to change the resize value inÂ generate.jsÂ andÂ train.js

  - **Why Customize:**Â Different video games have different aspect ratios and resolutions.

- **Patch Size (dit.js,Â vae.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â TheÂ patchSizeÂ parameter in bothÂ dit.jsÂ andÂ vae.jsÂ dictates the granularity of the patches used. The default value isÂ 2. You can change this.

  - **Why Customize:**Â Smaller patches may capture more detail, larger patches can provide a more global context but might loose fine details.

- **Number of FramesÂ (train.js,generate.js\`):**

  - **Customization:**Â TheÂ max_framesÂ (in the python script) and theÂ totalFramesÂ (inÂ train.js, andÂ generate.js) parameter dictates how many frames we should use.

  - **Why Customize:**Â You may have shorter or longer videos, and you may need to tweak these values so that the training and generation processes are more efficient and do not require padding.

- **Model Dimensions (dit.js,Â vae.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â Parameters likeÂ hiddenSize,Â depth,Â numHeads,Â enc_dim,Â dec_dimÂ andÂ latent_dimÂ control model size and capacity.

  - **Why Customize:**Â These parameters are very influential, and they determine the complexity and the capability of the model. Smaller models are better suited for browser training, however larger models might have better generalization.

- **Learning Rate (train.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â TheÂ learningRateÂ parameter affects the speed of convergence of the model and may need to be changed depending on the data, the size of the model, the batch size etc.

  - **Why Customize:**Â An optimal learning rate will help the model learn faster, and produce better results.

- **Number of Epochs (train.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â The number ofÂ epochsÂ determines how many times we iterate over the full dataset.

  - **Why Customize:**Â More epochs might produce better results, but if the model is overfitting, less epochs might produce better results.

- **VAE Reconstruction Weight (train.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â TheÂ vaeReconstructionWeightÂ is a hyper parameter that determines how much importance we give to the VAE loss.

  - **Why Customize**: You may need to tune this value to balance between diffusion performance, and the VAE reconstruction of the image.

- **Action Categories and Embeddings (utils.js,Â train.js):**

  - **Customization:**Â You'll need to customize theÂ ActionEmbedderÂ andÂ createActionEmbeddingÂ function to handle the specific action categories you want the model to understand.

  - **Why Customize:**Â The default version assumes a Minecraft-like input, and you may have a different set of actions.

**3. UI/UX**

- **index.htmlÂ (All styles, training setup, etc.):**

  - **Customization:**Â You may need to change the styling, the button behavior, and what is being displayed, to better suite your use-case.

  - **Why Customize**: The default version is very minimal and is provided only as a starting point.

**How to Identify Customization Points:**

1. **Specific Requirements:**Â Define what you're trying to achieve (e.g., which video game style you want to emulate, what actions are needed).

2. **Understand Input Data:**Â Analyze the format and structure of your video frames and action data.

3. **Map to Parameters:**Â Match your requirements to model parameters and script inputs.

4. **Iterate and Experiment:**Â Make changes, run the code, and observe the results. Adjust the parameters as needed.

By customizing these inputs, you can adapt the provided setup to train and generate videos from various sources, actions, model sizes, and more. It's a process of experimentation to find what works best for your specific scenario. Do you have any other questions?

```

    echo "Usage: $0 <youtube_url>"
    exit 1
fi

YOUTUBE_URL="$1"
...
```

- **if \[ -z "$1" \]; then ... fi**: This checks if the first argument passed to the script ($1) is empty (i.e., no URL was provided). If it's empty, it prints a usage message and exits.

- **YOUTUBE_URL="$1"**: This line assigns theÂ *first argument*Â you provide when running the script to the variableÂ YOUTUBE_URL.

- **yt-dlp -o "${VIDEO_PATH}" "$YOUTUBE_URL"**: This usesÂ yt-dlpÂ to download the video. TheÂ $YOUTUBE_URLÂ is where the video URL is used.

```
./setup.sh https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YOUR_VIDEO_ID
```

more_vert

Ah, I see the problem! The issue you're encountering is with how the shell is interpreting the ampersand (&) and other special characters in your YouTube URL. The shell sees theÂ &Â as an attempt to run the command in the background and the shell also sees the characters after that as a completely separate command.

To fix this, you need to wrap your YouTube URL inÂ **double quotes**Â when you pass it as an argument to theÂ setup.shÂ script. This will prevent the shell from misinterpreting the characters in the URL.

Here's the corrected way to run your command:

```
./setup.sh "https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=k28S26wMnVI&pp=ygUObWluZWNyYWZ0IGdhbWU%3D"
```

content_copy**download**

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Bash

**Key Change:**

- **Double Quotes:**Â I've enclosed the entire YouTube URL within double quotes:Â "...".

**Why This Works:**

- **Quoting:**Â Double quotes tell the shell to treat the entire enclosed string as a single argument, even if it contains special characters likeÂ &,Â =,Â ?, etc. Without the double quotes, the shell would seeÂ &Â as an instruction to run part of the URL as a separate command in the background, which is not what we want.

**Try This:**

Run the command with the double quotes, and it should fix the "no matches found" error and proceed with the script:

```
./setup.sh "https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=k28S26wMnVI&pp=ygUObWluZWNyYWZ0IGdhbWU%3D"
```

Use codeÂ **[with caution](https://support.google.com/legal/answer/13505487)**.Bash

edit

more_vert

Okay, it appears we've cleared the initial hurdle with the URL parsing, but now we're facing a new issue: the video download is failing despiteÂ yt-dlpÂ running without errors. The error message "Error: Video download failed." suggests that something went wrongÂ *after*Â yt-dlpÂ seemingly completed its task, and the files being created have a non standard name.

Let's analyze this:

1. **yt-dlpÂ Output:**Â TheÂ yt-dlpÂ output shows that it's downloading the video and merging the audio and video streams. This part seems to be working correctly. However, the name contains the extraÂ pp=ygUObWluZWNyYWZ0IGdhbWU3DÂ which indicates something is wrong.

2. **Error Message:**Â The "Error: Video download failed." message comesÂ *after*Â yt-dlpÂ finishes. The error is occurring because of this non standard name, which is not what the program expects.

Here's what I suspect is happening:

- **Filename Issue:**Â The YouTube URL is including theÂ &pp=ygUObWluZWNyYWZ0IGdhbWU%3DÂ part, which is not part of the video ID. This part of the URL is usually related to the YouTube search result that you clicked on. The filename generated byÂ yt-dlpÂ contains this unneeded section, and our code expects it to only have the video id.

**How to Fix This**

We need to extract the video ID only before we download the video. We can use a combination ofÂ sedÂ and string manipulation to do this directly in the script.

Let's modify theÂ setup.shÂ script:

```
#!/bin/bash

# Check if the user provided a YouTube URL
if [ -z "$1" ]; then
    echo "Usage: $0 <youtube_url>"
    exit 1
fi

YOUTUBE_URL="$1"
OUTPUT_DIR="sample_data"
# Extract only the video ID part from the URL
VIDEO_ID=$(echo "$YOUTUBE_URL" | sed 's/.*\/\(.*\)\(.*\)/\1/' | sed 's/[^a-zA-Z0-9_-]//g') #this should extract the correct ID
VIDEO_PATH="${OUTPUT_DIR}/${VIDEO_ID}.mp4"
FRAMES_DIR="${OUTPUT_DIR}/frames"
ACTION_FILE="${OUTPUT_DIR}/actions.json"
DATA_INDEX="${OUTPUT_DIR}/data_index.json"
HTML_FILE="index.html"

echo "Starting setup process..."

# 1. Ensure the output directory exists
mkdir -p "${OUTPUT_DIR}"

# 2. Download the YouTube Video
echo "Downloading video from: ${YOUTUBE_URL}"
if ! command -v yt-dlp &> /dev/null
then
    echo "yt-dlp could not be found, please install: pip install yt-dlp"
     exit 1
fi
yt-dlp -o "${VIDEO_PATH}" "$YOUTUBE_URL"

# Check if the download was successful
if [ ! -f "${VIDEO_PATH}" ]; then
    echo "Error: Video download failed."
    exit 1
fi

# 3. Extract Frames
echo "Extracting frames to: ${FRAMES_DIR}"
if ! command -v ffmpeg &> /dev/null
then
    echo "ffmpeg could not be found, please install: sudo apt install ffmpeg"
    exit 1
fi
ffmpeg -i "${VIDEO_PATH}" -vf "fps=4" "${FRAMES_DIR}/frame_%04d.png"

# Check if frames were extracted successfully
if [ ! -d "${FRAMES_DIR}" ] || [ "$(ls -A ${FRAMES_DIR})" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not extract the video frames."
   exit 1
fi


# 4. Create Dummy Action File (Replace this with real labeling or action extraction as necessary)
echo "Creating dummy action file: ${ACTION_FILE}"

echo '{"frame_0001.png": {"movement": [0, 0, 0, 0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}}' > $ACTION_FILE


# 5. Create Data Index (Modify paths and action file reading)
echo "Generating Data Index File: ${DATA_INDEX}"
python -c "
import os
import json

frame_dir = '${FRAMES_DIR}'
action_file = '${ACTION_FILE}'
output_file = '${DATA_INDEX}'
max_frames = 32
if not os.path.exists(action_file):
  action_data = {}
  for filename in os.listdir(frame_dir):
      action_data[filename] = {'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0}
else:
  with open(action_file, 'r') as f:
    action_data = json.load(f)

data_index = []
frame_files = sorted([f for f in os.listdir(frame_dir) if f.endswith('.png')])

for i in range(0, len(frame_files) - max_frames, max_frames):
    chunk_frames = frame_files[i:i+max_frames]
    chunk_actions = []
    for frame in chunk_frames:
        if frame in action_data:
           chunk_actions.append(action_data[frame])
        else:
          chunk_actions.append({'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0})
    data_index.append({
        'path': [os.path.join(frame_dir, frame) for frame in chunk_frames],
        'action': chunk_actions
    })
with open(output_file, 'w') as outfile:
    json.dump(data_index, outfile)
"

# Check if the data index was successfully created
if [ ! -f "${DATA_INDEX}" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not generate the data index."
   exit 1
fi
# 6. Create a Basic HTML UI
echo "Creating basic HTML UI: ${HTML_FILE}"

cat << EOF > "${HTML_FILE}"
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head>
    <title>Minecraft DiT Training</title>
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"></script>
    <style>
        body { font-family: sans-serif; padding: 20px; }
        #videoContainer { display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap; gap: 10px; }
        video { width: 300px; height: auto; }
        #generationContainer{margin-top: 20px}
        canvas{ width: 300px; height: auto;}
        button {margin-top: 10px; background-color: #4CAF50; color: white; padding: 10px 15px; border: none; cursor: pointer;}
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Minecraft DiT Training</h1>
      <h2>Video Input</h2>
        <div id="videoContainer"></div>
        <button id="trainButton">Start Training</button>
        <div id = "generationContainer"></div>
    <script type="module">
        import { train } from './train.js';
        import { generateVideo } from './generate.js'
        import {MinecraftDataset} from './dataset.js';
        const videoContainer = document.getElementById('videoContainer');
        const trainButton = document.getElementById("trainButton")
        const generationContainer = document.getElementById("generationContainer")
           const dataIndexResponse = await fetch("sample_data/data_index.json");
           const dataIndex = await dataIndexResponse.json();

        async function loadVideoFromPath(path){
            const video = await fetch(path);
            const buffer = await video.arrayBuffer()
            const bytes = new Uint8Array(buffer)
            const image = tf.browser.fromPixels(tf.tensor(bytes, [1, 1, 1, 1] ) , 3) //replace by actual shape
            return image;
        }

        function processActions(actions) {
          return actions
        }


        for(let d of dataIndex){
          let path = d.path[0];
         let video = document.createElement('video');
            video.controls = true;
            video.width = 300
            video.height = 200;
            video.src = path;
             videoContainer.appendChild(video);
        }


         trainButton.addEventListener("click", async() => {
              await train(dataIndex)
             let paths = dataIndex[0].path;
             let imagePaths = paths.slice(0, 1);
             let actions = dataIndex[0].action;

             let frames = [];
              for(let path of imagePaths){
               let image = await loadVideoFromPath(path);
               frames.push(image)
              }
             let tensor = tf.concat(frames, 0)

               let generated = await generateVideo(tensor, [actions])
               let canvas
               for(let frame of tf.unstack(generated[0], 0)){
                   canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
                   canvas.width = frame.shape[1]
                   canvas.height = frame.shape[0]
                   generationContainer.appendChild(canvas)
                   await tf.browser.toPixels(tf.clipByValue(frame, 0, 1), canvas)
               }
           })
    </script>
</body>
</html>
EOF

echo "Setup complete. Open ${HTML_FILE} in your browser."
```

more_vert

Okay, I see what's happening. It seems that even with the correctedÂ VIDEO_IDÂ extraction,Â yt-dlpÂ is still creating a file with an incorrect name because of the youtube url we are passing. The issue is still thatÂ yt-dlpÂ is downloading a file with a name it chooses, rather than letting us define the filename ourselves.

Here's the core problem, and how to fix it:

**Problem:**

- **yt-dlp's Output Formatting:**Â Even though we're now correctly extracting the video ID,Â yt-dlpÂ seems to beÂ *prepending*Â theÂ watchÂ segment when it decides on what output file to use.

- **Inconsistent Filenames:**Â The name is not what we specify inÂ VIDEO_PATH

- **Existing File:**Â If we run the command a second time, it complains that this file already exists, sinceÂ yt-dlpÂ uses the same name even if the url contains theÂ &pp=.

**Solution:**

- We must ensure that the file name is exactly what we specify. To do this, we can change theÂ -oÂ parameter to useÂ %()Â so that we can explicitly define what we want, and remove theÂ watchÂ parameter which is being automatically added.

Let's modify theÂ setup.shÂ script again to reflect this:

```
#!/bin/bash

# Check if the user provided a YouTube URL
if [ -z "$1" ]; then
    echo "Usage: $0 <youtube_url>"
    exit 1
fi

YOUTUBE_URL="$1"
OUTPUT_DIR="sample_data"
# Extract only the video ID part from the URL
VIDEO_ID=$(echo "$YOUTUBE_URL" | sed 's/.*\/\(.*\)\(.*\)/\1/' | sed 's/[^a-zA-Z0-9_-]//g')
VIDEO_PATH="${OUTPUT_DIR}/${VIDEO_ID}.mp4"
FRAMES_DIR="${OUTPUT_DIR}/frames"
ACTION_FILE="${OUTPUT_DIR}/actions.json"
DATA_INDEX="${OUTPUT_DIR}/data_index.json"
HTML_FILE="index.html"

echo "Starting setup process..."

# 1. Ensure the output directory exists
mkdir -p "${OUTPUT_DIR}"

# 2. Download the YouTube Video
echo "Downloading video from: ${YOUTUBE_URL}"
if ! command -v yt-dlp &> /dev/null
then
    echo "yt-dlp could not be found, please install: pip install yt-dlp"
     exit 1
fi
# Explicit filename with "%()" syntax
yt-dlp -o "${OUTPUT_DIR}/%(id)s.%(ext)s"  --no-part "$YOUTUBE_URL"

# Check if the download was successful
if [ ! -f "${VIDEO_PATH}" ]; then
    echo "Error: Video download failed."
    exit 1
fi

# 3. Extract Frames
echo "Extracting frames to: ${FRAMES_DIR}"
if ! command -v ffmpeg &> /dev/null
then
    echo "ffmpeg could not be found, please install: sudo apt install ffmpeg"
    exit 1
fi
ffmpeg -i "${VIDEO_PATH}" -vf "fps=4" "${FRAMES_DIR}/frame_%04d.png"

# Check if frames were extracted successfully
if [ ! -d "${FRAMES_DIR}" ] || [ "$(ls -A ${FRAMES_DIR})" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not extract the video frames."
   exit 1
fi


# 4. Create Dummy Action File (Replace this with real labeling or action extraction as necessary)
echo "Creating dummy action file: ${ACTION_FILE}"

echo '{"frame_0001.png": {"movement": [0, 0, 0, 0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}}' > $ACTION_FILE


# 5. Create Data Index (Modify paths and action file reading)
echo "Generating Data Index File: ${DATA_INDEX}"
python -c "
import os
import json

frame_dir = '${FRAMES_DIR}'
action_file = '${ACTION_FILE}'
output_file = '${DATA_INDEX}'
max_frames = 32
if not os.path.exists(action_file):
  action_data = {}
  for filename in os.listdir(frame_dir):
      action_data[filename] = {'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0}
else:
  with open(action_file, 'r') as f:
    action_data = json.load(f)

data_index = []
frame_files = sorted([f for f in os.listdir(frame_dir) if f.endswith('.png')])

for i in range(0, len(frame_files) - max_frames, max_frames):
    chunk_frames = frame_files[i:i+max_frames]
    chunk_actions = []
    for frame in chunk_frames:
        if frame in action_data:
           chunk_actions.append(action_data[frame])
        else:
          chunk_actions.append({'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0})
    data_index.append({
        'path': [os.path.join(frame_dir, frame) for frame in chunk_frames],
        'action': chunk_actions
    })
with open(output_file, 'w') as outfile:
    json.dump(data_index, outfile)
"

# Check if the data index was successfully created
if [ ! -f "${DATA_INDEX}" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not generate the data index."
   exit 1
fi
# 6. Create a Basic HTML UI
echo "Creating basic HTML UI: ${HTML_FILE}"

cat << EOF > "${HTML_FILE}"
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head>
    <title>Minecraft DiT Training</title>
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"></script>
    <style>
        body { font-family: sans-serif; padding: 20px; }
        #videoContainer { display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap; gap: 10px; }
        video { width: 300px; height: auto; }
        #generationContainer{margin-top: 20px}
        canvas{ width: 300px; height: auto;}
        button {margin-top: 10px; background-color: #4CAF50; color: white; padding: 10px 15px; border: none; cursor: pointer;}
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Minecraft DiT Training</h1>
      <h2>Video Input</h2>
        <div id="videoContainer"></div>
        <button id="trainButton">Start Training</button>
        <div id = "generationContainer"></div>
    <script type="module">
        import { train } from './train.js';
        import { generateVideo } from './generate.js'
        import {MinecraftDataset} from './dataset.js';
        const videoContainer = document.getElementById('videoContainer');
        const trainButton = document.getElementById("trainButton")
        const generationContainer = document.getElementById("generationContainer")
           const dataIndexResponse = await fetch("sample_data/data_index.json");
           const dataIndex = await dataIndexResponse.json();

        async function loadVideoFromPath(path){
            const video = await fetch(path);
            const buffer = await video.arrayBuffer()
            const bytes = new Uint8Array(buffer)
            const image = tf.browser.fromPixels(tf.tensor(bytes, [1, 1, 1, 1] ) , 3) //replace by actual shape
            return image;
        }

        function processActions(actions) {
          return actions
        }


        for(let d of dataIndex){
          let path = d.path[0];
         let video = document.createElement('video');
            video.controls = true;
            video.width = 300
            video.height = 200;
            video.src = path;
             videoContainer.appendChild(video);
        }


         trainButton.addEventListener("click", async() => {
              await train(dataIndex)
             let paths = dataIndex[0].path;
             let imagePaths = paths.slice(0, 1);
             let actions = dataIndex[0].action;

             let frames = [];
              for(let path of imagePaths){
               let image = await loadVideoFromPath(path);
               frames.push(image)
              }
             let tensor = tf.concat(frames, 0)

               let generated = await generateVideo(tensor, [actions])
               let canvas
               for(let frame of tf.unstack(generated[0], 0)){
                   canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
                   canvas.width = frame.shape[1]
                   canvas.height = frame.shape[0]
                   generationContainer.appendChild(canvas)
                   await tf.browser.toPixels(tf.clipByValue(frame, 0, 1), canvas)
               }
           })
    </script>
</body>
</html>
EOF

echo "Setup complete. Open ${HTML_FILE} in your browser."
```

You are absolutely right to call me out on this! My apologies, I keep missing subtle details about howÂ yt-dlpÂ handles filenames and how it interacts with the rest of the script. The issue we have now is that I removed the logic for removing theÂ watchÂ parameter, and we are still creating a file with the nameÂ sample_data/watchvk28S26wMnVIppygUObWluZWNyYWZ0IGdhbWU7D.mp4.webmÂ (or similar), which does not match what the rest of the script expects.

Let's fix this once and for all by:

1. **Extracting the Video ID:**Â We will keep the video id extraction that we added before.

2. **Explicit Filename**: We will ensure that we are passing a filename that exactly matches our expectation.

Here's the updatedÂ setup.shÂ that addresses this:

```
#!/bin/bash

# Check if the user provided a YouTube URL
if [ -z "$1" ]; then
    echo "Usage: $0 <youtube_url>"
    exit 1
fi

YOUTUBE_URL="$1"
OUTPUT_DIR="sample_data"
# Extract only the video ID part from the URL
VIDEO_ID=$(echo "$YOUTUBE_URL" | sed 's/.*\/\(.*\)\(.*\)/\1/' | sed 's/[^a-zA-Z0-9_-]//g')
VIDEO_PATH="${OUTPUT_DIR}/${VIDEO_ID}.mp4"
FRAMES_DIR="${OUTPUT_DIR}/frames"
ACTION_FILE="${OUTPUT_DIR}/actions.json"
DATA_INDEX="${OUTPUT_DIR}/data_index.json"
HTML_FILE="index.html"

echo "Starting setup process..."

# 1. Ensure the output directory exists
mkdir -p "${OUTPUT_DIR}"

# 2. Download the YouTube Video
echo "Downloading video from: ${YOUTUBE_URL}"
if ! command -v yt-dlp &> /dev/null
then
    echo "yt-dlp could not be found, please install: pip install yt-dlp"
     exit 1
fi
# Explicit filename using a specific name we are choosing (which is exactly ${VIDEO_PATH})
yt-dlp -o "${VIDEO_PATH}"  --no-part "$YOUTUBE_URL"

# Check if the download was successful
if [ ! -f "${VIDEO_PATH}" ]; then
    echo "Error: Video download failed."
    exit 1
fi

# 3. Extract Frames
echo "Extracting frames to: ${FRAMES_DIR}"
if ! command -v ffmpeg &> /dev/null
then
    echo "ffmpeg could not be found, please install: sudo apt install ffmpeg"
    exit 1
fi
ffmpeg -i "${VIDEO_PATH}" -vf "fps=4" "${FRAMES_DIR}/frame_%04d.png"

# Check if frames were extracted successfully
if [ ! -d "${FRAMES_DIR}" ] || [ "$(ls -A ${FRAMES_DIR})" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not extract the video frames."
   exit 1
fi


# 4. Create Dummy Action File (Replace this with real labeling or action extraction as necessary)
echo "Creating dummy action file: ${ACTION_FILE}"

echo '{"frame_0001.png": {"movement": [0, 0, 0, 0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}}' > $ACTION_FILE


# 5. Create Data Index (Modify paths and action file reading)
echo "Generating Data Index File: ${DATA_INDEX}"
python -c "
import os
import json

frame_dir = '${FRAMES_DIR}'
action_file = '${ACTION_FILE}'
output_file = '${DATA_INDEX}'
max_frames = 32
if not os.path.exists(action_file):
  action_data = {}
  for filename in os.listdir(frame_dir):
      action_data[filename] = {'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0}
else:
  with open(action_file, 'r') as f:
    action_data = json.load(f)

data_index = []
frame_files = sorted([f for f in os.listdir(frame_dir) if f.endswith('.png')])

for i in range(0, len(frame_files) - max_frames, max_frames):
    chunk_frames = frame_files[i:i+max_frames]
    chunk_actions = []
    for frame in chunk_frames:
        if frame in action_data:
           chunk_actions.append(action_data[frame])
        else:
          chunk_actions.append({'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0})
    data_index.append({
        'path': [os.path.join(frame_dir, frame) for frame in chunk_frames],
        'action': chunk_actions
    })
with open(output_file, 'w') as outfile:
    json.dump(data_index, outfile)
"

# Check if the data index was successfully created
if [ ! -f "${DATA_INDEX}" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not generate the data index."
   exit 1
fi
# 6. Create a Basic HTML UI
echo "Creating basic HTML UI: ${HTML_FILE}"

cat << EOF > "${HTML_FILE}"
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head>
    <title>Minecraft DiT Training</title>
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"></script>
    <style>
        body { font-family: sans-serif; padding: 20px; }
        #videoContainer { display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap; gap: 10px; }
        video { width: 300px; height: auto; }
        #generationContainer{margin-top: 20px}
        canvas{ width: 300px; height: auto;}
        button {margin-top: 10px; background-color: #4CAF50; color: white; padding: 10px 15px; border: none; cursor: pointer;}
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Minecraft DiT Training</h1>
      <h2>Video Input</h2>
        <div id="videoContainer"></div>
        <button id="trainButton">Start Training</button>
        <div id = "generationContainer"></div>
    <script type="module">
        import { train } from './train.js';
        import { generateVideo } from './generate.js'
        import {MinecraftDataset} from './dataset.js';
        const videoContainer = document.getElementById('videoContainer');
        const trainButton = document.getElementById("trainButton")
        const generationContainer = document.getElementById("generationContainer")
           const dataIndexResponse = await fetch("sample_data/data_index.json");
           const dataIndex = await dataIndexResponse.json();

        async function loadVideoFromPath(path){
            const video = await fetch(path);
            const buffer = await video.arrayBuffer()
            const bytes = new Uint8Array(buffer)
            const image = tf.browser.fromPixels(tf.tensor(bytes, [1, 1, 1, 1] ) , 3) //replace by actual shape
            return image;
        }

        function processActions(actions) {
          return actions
        }


        for(let d of dataIndex){
          let path = d.path[0];
         let video = document.createElement('video');
            video.controls = true;
            video.width = 300
            video.height = 200;
            video.src = path;
             videoContainer.appendChild(video);
        }


         trainButton.addEventListener("click", async() => {
              await train(dataIndex)
             let paths = dataIndex[0].path;
             let imagePaths = paths.slice(0, 1);
             let actions = dataIndex[0].action;

             let frames = [];
              for(let path of imagePaths){
               let image = await loadVideoFromPath(path);
               frames.push(image)
              }
             let tensor = tf.concat(frames, 0)

               let generated = await generateVideo(tensor, [actions])
               let canvas
               for(let frame of tf.unstack(generated[0], 0)){
                   canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
                   canvas.width = frame.shape[1]
                   canvas.height = frame.shape[0]
                   generationContainer.appendChild(canvas)
                   await tf.browser.toPixels(tf.clipByValue(frame, 0, 1), canvas)
               }
           })
    </script>
</body>
</html>
EOF

echo "Setup complete. Open ${HTML_FILE} in your browser."
```

more_vert

You are absolutely correct! It seems I'm having a persistent issue withÂ yt-dlpÂ and how it manages file names. I apologize for the continued trouble. It seems that theÂ --no-partÂ flag is preventing the download from happening again, and we also still have the problem of theÂ watchÂ being added to the filename.

Let's try a different approach that focuses on explicitly defining the output path and ensuring thatÂ yt-dlpÂ doesn't try to generate a different name using theÂ %(id)sÂ specifier. We'll also add a check to avoid downloading the video if it already exists.

Here's the modifiedÂ setup.shÂ script:

```
#!/bin/bash

# Check if the user provided a YouTube URL
if [ -z "$1" ]; then
    echo "Usage: $0 <youtube_url>"
    exit 1
fi

YOUTUBE_URL="$1"
OUTPUT_DIR="sample_data"
# Extract only the video ID part from the URL
VIDEO_ID=$(echo "$YOUTUBE_URL" | sed 's/.*\/\(.*\)\(.*\)/\1/' | sed 's/[^a-zA-Z0-9_-]//g')
VIDEO_PATH="${OUTPUT_DIR}/${VIDEO_ID}.mp4"
FRAMES_DIR="${OUTPUT_DIR}/frames"
ACTION_FILE="${OUTPUT_DIR}/actions.json"
DATA_INDEX="${OUTPUT_DIR}/data_index.json"
HTML_FILE="index.html"

echo "Starting setup process..."

# 1. Ensure the output directory exists
mkdir -p "${OUTPUT_DIR}"

# 2. Download the YouTube Video
echo "Downloading video from: ${YOUTUBE_URL}"
if ! command -v yt-dlp &> /dev/null
then
    echo "yt-dlp could not be found, please install: pip install yt-dlp"
     exit 1
fi

# Check if the video already exists
if [ -f "${VIDEO_PATH}" ]; then
    echo "Video already exists at: ${VIDEO_PATH}. Skipping download."
else
    # Explicit filename using a specific name we are choosing (which is exactly ${VIDEO_PATH})
    yt-dlp -o "${VIDEO_PATH}"  "$YOUTUBE_URL"
    # Check if the download was successful
    if [ ! -f "${VIDEO_PATH}" ]; then
      echo "Error: Video download failed."
      exit 1
    fi
fi


# 3. Extract Frames
echo "Extracting frames to: ${FRAMES_DIR}"
if ! command -v ffmpeg &> /dev/null
then
    echo "ffmpeg could not be found, please install: sudo apt install ffmpeg"
    exit 1
fi
ffmpeg -i "${VIDEO_PATH}" -vf "fps=4" "${FRAMES_DIR}/frame_%04d.png"

# Check if frames were extracted successfully
if [ ! -d "${FRAMES_DIR}" ] || [ "$(ls -A ${FRAMES_DIR})" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not extract the video frames."
   exit 1
fi


# 4. Create Dummy Action File (Replace this with real labeling or action extraction as necessary)
echo "Creating dummy action file: ${ACTION_FILE}"

echo '{"frame_0001.png": {"movement": [0, 0, 0, 0], "camera": [0, 0], "interaction": 0}}' > $ACTION_FILE


# 5. Create Data Index (Modify paths and action file reading)
echo "Generating Data Index File: ${DATA_INDEX}"
python -c "
import os
import json

frame_dir = '${FRAMES_DIR}'
action_file = '${ACTION_FILE}'
output_file = '${DATA_INDEX}'
max_frames = 32
if not os.path.exists(action_file):
  action_data = {}
  for filename in os.listdir(frame_dir):
      action_data[filename] = {'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0}
else:
  with open(action_file, 'r') as f:
    action_data = json.load(f)

data_index = []
frame_files = sorted([f for f in os.listdir(frame_dir) if f.endswith('.png')])

for i in range(0, len(frame_files) - max_frames, max_frames):
    chunk_frames = frame_files[i:i+max_frames]
    chunk_actions = []
    for frame in chunk_frames:
        if frame in action_data:
           chunk_actions.append(action_data[frame])
        else:
          chunk_actions.append({'movement': [0, 0, 0, 0], 'camera': [0, 0], 'interaction': 0})
    data_index.append({
        'path': [os.path.join(frame_dir, frame) for frame in chunk_frames],
        'action': chunk_actions
    })
with open(output_file, 'w') as outfile:
    json.dump(data_index, outfile)
"

# Check if the data index was successfully created
if [ ! -f "${DATA_INDEX}" ]; then
   echo "Error: could not generate the data index."
   exit 1
fi
# 6. Create a Basic HTML UI
echo "Creating basic HTML UI: ${HTML_FILE}"

cat << EOF > "${HTML_FILE}"
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head>
    <title>Minecraft DiT Training</title>
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tensorflow/tfjs@latest"></script>
    <style>
        body { font-family: sans-serif; padding: 20px; }
        #videoContainer { display: flex; flex-wrap: wrap; gap: 10px; }
        video { width: 300px; height: auto; }
        #generationContainer{margin-top: 20px}
        canvas{ width: 300px; height: auto;}
        button {margin-top: 10px; background-color: #4CAF50; color: white; padding: 10px 15px; border: none; cursor: pointer;}
    </style>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Minecraft DiT Training</h1>
      <h2>Video Input</h2>
        <div id="videoContainer"></div>
        <button id="trainButton">Start Training</button>
        <div id = "generationContainer"></div>
    <script type="module">
        import { train } from './train.js';
        import { generateVideo } from './generate.js'
        import {MinecraftDataset} from './dataset.js';
        const videoContainer = document.getElementById('videoContainer');
        const trainButton = document.getElementById("trainButton")
        const generationContainer = document.getElementById("generationContainer")
           const dataIndexResponse = await fetch("sample_data/data_index.json");
           const dataIndex = await dataIndexResponse.json();

        async function loadVideoFromPath(path){
            const video = await fetch(path);
            const buffer = await video.arrayBuffer()
            const bytes = new Uint8Array(buffer)
            const image = tf.browser.fromPixels(tf.tensor(bytes, [1, 1, 1, 1] ) , 3) //replace by actual shape
            return image;
        }

        function processActions(actions) {
          return actions
        }


        for(let d of dataIndex){
          let path = d.path[0];
         let video = document.createElement('video');
            video.controls = true;
            video.width = 300
            video.height = 200;
            video.src = path;
             videoContainer.appendChild(video);
        }


         trainButton.addEventListener("click", async() => {
              await train(dataIndex)
             let paths = dataIndex[0].path;
             let imagePaths = paths.slice(0, 1);
             let actions = dataIndex[0].action;

             let frames = [];
              for(let path of imagePaths){
               let image = await loadVideoFromPath(path);
               frames.push(image)
              }
             let tensor = tf.concat(frames, 0)

               let generated = await generateVideo(tensor, [actions])
               let canvas
               for(let frame of tf.unstack(generated[0], 0)){
                   canvas = document.createElement('canvas');
                   canvas.width = frame.shape[1]
                   canvas.height = frame.shape[0]
                   generationContainer.appendChild(canvas)
                   await tf.browser.toPixels(tf.clipByValue(frame, 0, 1), canvas)
               }
           })
    </script>
</body>
</html>
EOF

echo "Setup complete. Open ${HTML_FILE} in your browser."
```
